    <li> Like most other reviewers here, I have been disappointed in the past with mirrors that claimed to be fog-free but that would only stay that way for a couple of weeks at best. On the other hand, I have been using this mirror almost two months and it is just as fog-free as when I got it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE: I dropped my review from five to four stars because after a while, the mirror got hazy and I was unable to restore it to its original clarity even with toothpaste. Still, for the price the mirror lasted about a year, maybe more, which is much longer than any other shaving mirror I&#x27;ve used in the past.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Actually, the mirror does get fogged--however, unlike other shower mirrors, this one has a small slot cut out in its upper center portion that allows it to be hung on the included adhesive hook. When it does fog up, you simply remove it, run it under your shower water for a second or two, and place it back on the hook--and it&#x27;s good to go for 3-5 more minutes. I recently started shaving in the shower and I do 2-3 passes, and I&#x27;ve found that one rinse is good enough for an entire pass. So, a quick rinse between passes is all I need to get a babyface. This not only saves time, but cuts down on the razor irritation, nicks and cuts as well. This mirror is also ideal for washing your face. I use a facial cleanser in a tube and this mirror helps me get a nice even lather all over my face and keeps me from missing any spots.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The hook included with the mirror is easy to install and it&#x27;s very sturdy--it has not budged since I put it up.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you have a small shower and/or stuff all over the place inside it, this mirror won&#x27;t cause too much crowding. I&#x27;m not sure offhand what the dimensions are, but it&#x27;s just big enough for my face and doesn&#x27;t take up much room at all.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Another reviewer commented about water spots. They do accumulate over time, but the directions suggested cleaning them with toothpaste, which works like a champ. It made my spotted mirror look brand new again.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Oh, and one other thing, just to echo other reviewers: there is a strip of plastic covering the mirror that needs to be removed before use. It&#x27;s a bit tricky to get a purchase on, and you might think you&#x27;re removing something that&#x27;s supposed to be there. Once you get a hold of it, though, it comes off pretty easily.</li>
    <li> It is wonderful.....it really works and it&#x27;s safe for my grandaughter when she visits, she loves it. My husband uses for shaving, said it really works well. I liked the price.AMAZON RULES if AMAZON DOESN&#x27;T HAVE IT YOU CAN&#x27;T BUY IT, THAT GOES FOR EVERYTHING I LOOK FOR</li>

    <li> Like several other reviews, I was kind of surprised at the small size (probably because I didn&#x27;t pay any attention to the dimensions in the product description), but upon climbing in the shower in order to decide where to mount the hook, I quickly discovered that it is just the right size for the task at hand (unless for some strange reason you like to stand 3 feet away when shaving)!  My shower is the type that is located in a tub enclosure, so after trying out a couple of placements I decided to mount it at the opposite end of the shower head.  This works out just great since all I have to do is make a 180 degree turn and I can shave without having the shower stream interfere with the view of my handsome mug!    I also really like the design of this item compared to all the competition.  It is total simplicity.  But after reading reviews on 6 or 7 other allegedly fog free mirrors I came to see that in this particular case simple is much more practical than complicated (and expensive).  As advertised, it stayed fog free after holding it under the shower stream for 3-4 seconds!    Lastly, I must mention the incredible customer service that this company offers with this product.  Shortly after ordering this item I received an e-mail from a representative of the company thanking me and telling me about the product, and how to get started by removing the protective cover.  Never in my life have I seen or heard of such amazing customer service, and certainly would not have expected in my wildest dreams to receive it from a $10 purchase!  Bravo and Kudos to the Cumberland Company!!  I wish they made more things because I would definitely buy from them!!!</li>
    <li> I had read other reviews about the size of the mirror. Not sure what others are talking about but the mirror size is perfect for the shower. I shave both my head and face in the shower and have no problems seeing my entire face and head when I shave. I also have had no fogging issues at all. Simply run the mirror under the water as directed and no fog! Many times I don&#x27;t even have to run water over it before I shave. I think this is a great product and would recommend it to anybody. Thanks!</li>
    <li> I really, really hate shaving. When I&#x27;m not out of town on business trips I won&#x27;t shave at all. I hate being scruffy and unshaven but I really hate standing there in the cold trying to shave too. Shower mirrors make this process much easier. Unlike other shower mirrors this does not attach to the water line, nor does it have an anti-fog coating (these generally start to peel off after a few uses). It becomes fog free by holding the mirror under hot water for a few seconds. This keeps the mirror fog-less long enough to shave. I think that this anti-fog method is likely the most effective, its also the least expensive.</li>
    <li> Great mirror, does it&#x27;s job nicely</li>
    <li> The mirror is indeed very small. But we got this for our 7 year old so he can see himself and check his hair as he is shampooing. (He tends to miss parts of his hair when he is shampooing.) The mirror is crystal clear and fogless. However, the only reason I give it 3 stars is because it does NOT stick to the wall. It comes with something similar to the 3M hooks, but it&#x27;s the dollar store kind and the hold on it is not good. If you want this to stick to the wall you will need to go buy a 3M hook. But I think it&#x27;s worth it, if this mirror is what you are looking for.</li>
    <li> I bought this for my husband and he loves it.  The hook is really great and hasn&#x27;t fallen off the wall once.  While the mirror is small (4x6), he says it&#x27;s perfect.     <li> This is a very small mirror. I have not figured out if its a good or bad thing that it sticks with an adhesive rather then a suction cup. But as far as fogging goes,It fogs up like every other mirror on the market. You have to throw water on it to defog.   Its not worth $9.99.   $4.99 maybe.     <li> Acrylic mirror with plastic hook plus adhesive strip.    You just hold it under the water to heat it up and it stays fog-free long enough to shave.     <li> I bought this for my very picky husband.  He regularly shaves in the shower, and likes having a mirror.  He&#x27;s bought several (many?) mirrors over the years - including at least one that cost close to $100.  None worked. I decided that, for the $10 this one cost, it was worth a try.  He (and I) were pleasantly surprised.  This one works well.  I did have to convince him to be patient enough to run it under the hot shower water for a few seconds, (maybe up to 10 seconds?)  so that it could become, and stay, fog free.  As they say, it works on basic science (fog is condensation and is drawn to cooler surfaces - warm it under the shower and no fog). While he initially wasn&#x27;t excited about that part, I was able to convince him that it was worth the (minimal) time - and certainly less time than he used to spend spraying things that didn&#x27;t work on mirrors in an attempt to restore coatings that didn&#x27;t work.  Several reviewers have commented on the small size.  My husband has a &#x27;less than small&#x27; face - and once he got used to the mirror size admitted it wasn&#x27;t an issue for him at all.  It adheres well to our ceramic tile shower.  Definitely recommend this mirror -</li>
    <li> Works as expected and well worth the Price.  Sometimes it has to be &#x27;heated up&#x27; twice to complete shaving.  What a hassle huh?!  Good product.</li>

    <li> Ok so ... at first I wasn&#x27;t too thrilled with the mirror and actually wrote a review here reflecting my dissatisfaction.  But within about an hour, I received a nicely worded email from the manufacturer offering insight to exactly how the technology in the mirrors construction, makes it truly fogless.  We had it positioned in the shower too high on the wall (have kids so ... glass and water + kids &#x3D; not good).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve posted this info below but I gotta say .... any company that is that willing to stand behind their product and offer such personal customer service is a 100% winner in my book.  If only all online retailers could be this way.  It&#x27;s nice to know they care enough to respond personally.  Buy the mirror ... it&#x27;s affordable and does what it says.  Enjoy!  :)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;From the email I received .......&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If I may, please allow me the opportunity to share how the mirror works in an attempt to help alleviate the fogging issues you mentioned in your review.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;  Most houses are kept in a temperature range of 70-75 degrees.&lt;br /&gt;  The average shower water temperature is 107.5 degrees.&lt;br /&gt;  Fog on a mirror is simply condensation. The air in the bathroom is heated by the shower and becomes saturated with moisture.&lt;br /&gt;  When this saturated moist hot air comes in contact with the shower shave mirror (which is still at normal room temperature roughly 30 degrees less), the moisture comes out of the air and condensates on the shower shave mirror surface.&lt;br /&gt;  When you hold you Shave Well mirror under the shower stream for a few seconds, the acrylic mirror will warm up allowing for the temperature of the moist air and the mirror itself to equalize.&lt;br /&gt;  Once you have held the mirror in the shower spray to equalize the temperature of you shower and the mirror, there can&#x27;t/won&#x27;t be any fog/condensation.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All of that being said, the mirror works on basic science.  If your mirror is still fogging then the only answer I can give you is that it remains cooler than the temperature of the shower.  Since the mirror is rather thin acrylic, it should warm up in the few seconds you have been holding it in the warm water of the shower spray.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Some additional thoughts that remain would be&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;a.) Whether or not you have a greatly reduced flow shower head.  If you do, it may take longer for enough warm water to equalize the temperature of the mirror.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;b.) If the mirror hung so high that there is a direct flow of cool air over the shower curtain/door or whether an air conditioning vent is blowing toward it.  If this is the case, I am happy to send you a new hook so that you can reposition the mirror.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;c.) One additional suggestion would be to make sure you are turning both the front and back of the mirror under the shower water spray when you are equalizing it.  This will help in \\&quot;warming it up\\&quot; to equalize the temperature.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Finally, regarding the issue of the size of the Shave Well mirror, it was designed to be removable from the wall to truly address the issue of fog by \\&quot;warming up\\&quot; the mirror under the shower. Given that the mirror will be removed from the hook before you shave, many users choose to hold the mirror while shaving. The 6\\&quot; X 4\\&quot; size fits well in a users hand as well as provides a complete reflection of the entire face while shaving.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;To avoid any confusion, under the Product Description section of the amazon.com listing is the size of the item is shown: \\&quot;The Shave Well Company fog free shower shave mirror measures 4\\&quot; wide, 6\\&quot; tall and is 1/8\\&quot; thick. The base of the adhesive hook (the part that sticks to the wall) measures 1\\&quot; wide and 1 1/2\\&quot; tall.\\&quot;u is that it remains cooler than the temperature of the shower.     <li> This is a simply mirror that comes with one of those white hooks that you peel the back off of to hang. The mirror has a gray back-side which I assume is meant to be sensitive to temperature? The premise is good I suppose. Why do mirrors fog in the shower? Because they are cold and collect water vapor / steam and condensation. The idea is that this mirror heats up quickly by running it under the hot shower water? First problem: I don&#x27;t have an extra hand to hold the mirror under the hot water in the shower, because I&#x27;m using both hands to wash myself. So, my answer was to take the mirror off the hook and set it on the ground in the shower so the \\&quot;runoff\\&quot; water would heat it up. Second problem: If you get the mirror warmed up so it won&#x27;t collect steam / condensation, it only stays heated up for a very short time (not long enough for me to shave before it starts steaming over again). Third problem: if I set the mirror on the floor of the shower to heat up, it collects soap scum and such very quickly (due to being exposed to runoff water). My assessment: I wasted my money on this product and I should have either bought a better made mirror (perhaps with a suction cup to hang it so I can move where it&#x27;s hanging) and deal with the steam, or I should have bought one of the more expensive mirrors that use an actual source water source to heat up the mirror.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;NOTE: Initially I gave this product 1 star, but I have since changed it to 3 stars. As others have noted, this seller really believes in his product, and that counts for something. Also, I&#x27;m still using it after some time now, so it can&#x27;t be all THAT bad. I really think the problems I experienced are the particularly cold initial temperature in my shower. The science here isn&#x27;t revolutionary (warm up the mirror, less condensation), but the basics of it are sound. I just have to keep \\&quot;re-warming\\&quot; periodically while I shave.</li>

    <li> I researched fogless shower mirrors a fair bit before purchasing this one.  The basic reason for fog, as one quickly finds out, is condensation due to temperature difference.  There are thus a few different ways of solving the problem.  One is for the mirror to be electrically heated.  Another is a hot water bank behind the mirror.  Another is a special coating on the mirror to attempt to slow temperature changes and condensation.  This mirror uses the simplest method possible, namely it hangs on a hook and you take it off and run it under the hot water.  I believe it is very effective.  Some people comment on its size.  That has never been a problem for me.  In fact, because it&#x27;s small enough, I would even consider bringing it on trips with me so I can shave in hotel showers.</li>

    <li> My search for a fog free mirror is officially over.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Simplicity is the key here. Attach the provided hook to the glass (better than attaching to tile) of the shower wall, and hang this mirror on it. When you&#x27;re ready to shave, take the mirror off the hook and hold it under the running hot water for about five seconds. This makes the mirror the same temp as the water, and thus impossible to fog up (steam results from temperature differences between a surface and the air; if they&#x27;re the SAME temp, it cannot form). It seems like a cheap trick to run it under water, because running water will wash away the fog from ANY mirror. However, because this mirror is thin, it retains the heat and remains at the water temp for quite some time. Other mirrors quickly cool off and form fog again. This one does not, at least not over the next five minutes. I guess if you left if hanging for 15 minutes fog would form again, but that&#x27;s beside the point. If it takes you that long between your decision to shave and the actual act, then you need to enroll in a time management class.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Complaints I have read re: Size. It is kind of small at 4\\&quot;  x 6\\&quot;. Having said that, it is PLENTY large enough to see my entire face to shave. Plus, even if it were not, I&#x27;m only shaving my lower face, and it is generous enough to show that. Unless your head is the size of Herman Munster&#x27;s, you&#x27;ll have plenty of room to see your ugly mug to remove that nasty hair and make yourself handsome again.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Re: falling off the wall. Yeah, mine did that too. Simple fix is to use shower/tub clear silicone caulk ($5 at a hardware store), put a dab onto the back of the wall hook, stick to the shower glass and let it sit overnight, and you&#x27;re done. It won&#x27;t fall of again. So, this is a non-issue.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I made mine even better by applying three coats of Rain-X (yes, the stuff you put on your windshield to force water beads to stay as beads instead of running together; if you do not own this product, you ought to because it&#x27;s the very best automotive product I&#x27;ve used and does exactly what it says). With it applied, after I put the mirror under the water, the water that remains on the surface beads up nicely, so I am not looking through smudged water streaks trying to see my skin. It&#x27;s a miracle product this Rain-X stuff. I use it on my car every month and don&#x27;t even bother turning my windshield wipers on when it rains. That&#x27;s how GREAT it is.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So, if you follow the very simple instructions, it works. Best of all? It cannot fail, because there are no moving parts, no electric components, no pieces to fit together, etc. Run it under hot water and enjoy fog free shaving. That&#x27;s all there is to it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you get it and don&#x27;t like it, return it. But if you don&#x27;t like it, then the problem is likely with you and not this simple-to-use product that performs exactly as advertised. In my experience, that is very rare indeed.very best automotive product I&#x27;ve used and does exactly what it says).     <li> A few years ago I was gifted a shower shaving mirror and have been hooked on shaving in the shower ever since. As compared to the old shave-over-the-bathroom-sink method, the steamy shower environment really seems to make the shaving experience smoother, faster and much less painful.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;That first shower mirror was the type held to the wall by a couple suction cups... and those cups became hard and lost their grip in about six months.  After that I tried a different mirror with four suction cups, and that one lasted about one year... actually had two of those in a row. Still, it would have been nice not to have had to purchase a replacement every nine to 12 months.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A couple months ago I went looking for a longer-term replacement, and reviews of this Shave Well shaving mirror seems to indicate that it might be exactly what was needed. I made the purchase and would say that those reviews were right on the mark; am very happy with this item&#x27;s functionality and mirrored surface, and offer the following for your consideration:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* Following instruction, I cleaned the shower wall very well and then allowed more than the noted 1 hour for the wall to dry&lt;br /&gt;* Mounted the mirror&#x27;s hook on the clean wall and allowed the adhesion to bond overnight before hanging the mirror&lt;br /&gt;* I shave near shower&#x27;s end by applying shaving gel, running the mirror under the water, hanging the mirror, and shaving&lt;br /&gt;* Putting the mirror under the water too early gave it time to cool, and fog returned. I now wait until ready to shave&lt;br /&gt;* Before leaving the shower I&#x27;ll shake the mirror to remove excess water, and might pat it once, not rub it, with the towel&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One thing I learned with the first few mirrors was how not to clean water spots from them... the first couple times I tried using dish soap and a scrubber sponge or a washcloth, and basically destroyed the mirrored finish on these things. None of the shower &#x27;mirrors&#x27; I have owned have actually been made of a glass mirror; instead, they seem to be made by applying a thin mirrored finished to a plastic or plexiglass backing.  That finish is fairly easy to damage, so some care is needed when trying to clean them.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;For whatever reason (maybe she read the instructions...) my wife suggested using toothpaste and that has worked quite well. For us, the paste type toothpaste works better than the gel type; we just apply a small dab or two, lightly rub the toothpaste around the mirror in small circles using the pad of our finger (not the fingernail), and then rinse it all off with warm water. Works amazingly well.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After a few months use - so far, so good. This mirror has been excellent and easy to use. If you are looking for a mirror for use similar to what I&#x27;ve expressed above, and looking for a product that will do the job without breaking the bank, then I highly recommend this too you. Photo #4: The back of the mirror is covered with thin thermal coating.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Fog forms on mirrors because of condensation. The water in shower is warmer than the air in the house, it warms the air in the bathroom and condensates on any cool surfaces such as mirrors. If you hold this thin mirror under water for 10 seconds to warm it up condensation does not form on the glass until the mirror cools off. I measured that it stayed fog free for about 13 minutes, then a quick dip into the hot shower and it was fog free again.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The best place to position the mirror is away from drafts that will quicken its cooling, and away from direct shower spray to minimize water spots.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall I am very pleased with the mirror and recommend it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Ali Julia reviewvery pleased with the mirror and recommend it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Ali Julia review</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve owned one of these for 2.5 years.  I&#x27;ve used both the regular and the deluxe size of this mirror. A piece of acrylic, with the mirror surface on the back side of the acrylic (which makes it sensitive to scratching.. see below).  Not much to it.  If you have a drafty shower, it will fog up significantly faster..  Also, I use a cheap suction cup + plastic hook that I picked up at Target, rather than the included hook (which uses some double-sided foam tape).  Mostly because I was going to be traveling with the thing and moving it around.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve dropped the mirror in a tile shower from 5+ feet DOZENS of times, and it&#x27;s still in one piece. If you push it around on hard surfaces, it will totally scratch.  It&#x27;s nothing to really be surpised about, but just be aware, if you happen to throw it lazily into a travel bag, etc.  Since the back (reflective mirror material) side isn&#x27;t protected, you could wind up with scratches in the mirror image.  Mine got a few scratches from me treating it like it was indestructible, so I now treat it much nicer.  Just saying.  The simplicity and the &amp;#34;fogless&amp;#34; feature has the drawback of the unprotected surfaces, so just be careful with it.  If you put it in your shower, and never move it, it will not scratch.  You literally need to be putting it on hard surfaces, etc, or where it can rub against hard stuff.  I move mine around between showers, traveling, etc, so it has seen more mileage than most, I&#x27;m sure.  Again, I&#x27;ve owned one for 2.5 years, and in that time, it picked up 2 scratches in the actual mirror material (shows up at thin black lines when looking in the mirror), and a few scratches on the front.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Yes, it will collect water droplets, when you rinse it / warm it up.  If you are so inclined, you could wax the surface with car wax, or something..?  No idea how that would hold up in the long run..  I surely didn&#x27;t do that!  For me, if there are way too many water droplets, I put it into the shower stream again, and try for a less obvious pattern.  I really don&#x27;t notice the droplets after a moment, though.  I also have hard water, and the mirror hasn&#x27;t had any problems with water marks, and I&#x27;ve never needed to or attempted to clean it..  Maybe the near-daily rinse keeps it fresh.</li>

The last move was sixteen years ago, and the manfacturer seems to have gone out of business--probably because their product lasted too long.     <li> I followed the instructions to the letter (the ones included with the produce and the ones emailed to me by the seller), but their fog free solution did not work for me.     <li> I used to shave in the shower by using a typical handheld mirror flipped upside down and placed carefully on a wall mounted razor holder.     <li> Shaving in the shower definitely makes for a smoother and closer shave. The trade-off is that you may be wasting a fair amount of water while doing so. On the other hand, turning off the water flow while shaving can make for a rather cold experience and negate the comfort benefit of a smooth and close shave. By installing a shower fixture with separate temperature and volume controls I&#x27;ve been able to minimize that drawback, since I can reduce water flow to a minimum while maintaining the proper temperature. Having done so, I can speak to the effectiveness of this mirror in a guilt-free manner. Also, it is easy to re-warm the mirror if a cooler air-stream hits it while shaving.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Customer communication and service is superb; I received an informative email even before delivery of the mirror, and printed information accompanying the mirror is clear and well-designed. Unlike most companies, the ShaveWell Company really means it when they say that customer delight with their product is the most important thing. Take a look at what other reviewers have to say about their prompt and helpful responses to customer questions.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Con&#x27;s (Minor):&lt;br /&gt;The mirror is fairly small - Depending on how your shower/bath stall configuration impacts where you hang it (and your eyesight), you might need to stand out ofthe shower flow in order to use it while it is hanging. If so, that can make for a chilly experience. My preference is to hang it far enough from the main water flow to minimize soapy spray that would lead to residue build-up, and in my small shower stall I can do so yet remain in a warm water flow.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Water remains beaded up on the mirror after warming it - Shaving visibilty remains OK, but it would be nice if the mirror was coated with a product that enables water to run-off such as those used on auto windshields and glass shower/bath doors.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Easily scratchable - Acrylic is clearly the safe choice for an in-shower mirror, but you need to exercise care when cleaning it. Should some soap scum eventually build up, be sure to use the proper cleaning agent and a soft cloth.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall Assessment:&lt;br /&gt;An inexpensive product that does what it promises from a company that truly cares about its customers. Big quality of life boost if you can minimize water waste / guilt. I would give it 5 stars if it came in a slightly larger size with a coating that enables water beads to run off.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update: SIMPLE TOOTHPASTE METHOD FOR REDUCING WATER BEADING - I tried the toothpaste suggestion for treating the mirror emailed to me from the Shave Well Company immediately after posting my review (and originally suggested by another reviewer) and found that it works quite well for minimizing water beading on the mirror during use. Simply wet the mirror, gently rub it with a pea-sized bit of toothpaste, rinse off, and repeat as needed. An additional benefit is that it delays soap scum build-up. I would suggest using a plain, inexpensive toothpaste instead of the fancy \\&quot;whitening\\&quot; toothpastes, which often contain fine polishing granules that might scratch the acrylic mirror.</li>

    <li> I don&#x27;t usually write reviews on Amazon, but I felt I had no choice in this matter. I gave this product 5 stars and I&#x27;ll explain why. After reading reviews for other fog resistant mirrors, I was weary about buying ANY of them. The thing that sets this mirror apart from others that I looked at are two things; one, the hanging method is secure and stable, but designed so that the mirror can be easily lifted off at any time, which is important because two, it needs to be removable to truly achieve a fog free surface. The company uses a simple explanation of how the mirror does this using basic science. Basically you just have to lift the mirror off and let the shower water hit both sides for a few seconds. When you do, the mirror&#x27;s surface temperature rises to match the room temperature and condensation will no longer stick to the surface. It sounds weird, but it works EXTREMELY well and the mirror stays fog free more than enough time to complete a shave. Due to its plastic design, the water beads up nicely on the front of this mirror, which impairs your vision to boot.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;What you have here is a plastic mirror worth about $0.55, a plastic hook with adhesive worth about $0.15, a thin protection sheet worth about $0.05, and a colorful printed box and instructions worth about $0.25 (all in bulk). The marketing team behind this mirror spends at least twice that amount per mirror in advertising and hype.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here&#x27;s a little clue - ANY mirror is &amp;#34;fog free&amp;#34; if you run it under the shower water to warm it up. I find it very hard to believe there are that many people happy paying $10 for something you could find at a dollar store that works just as well. Heck, you could even use the broken shard of a truck stop mirror stuck to your shower wall with the piece of gum you found on the bathroom stall and it would be exactly as &amp;#34;fog free by design&amp;#34; as this mirror. I have had mine fall twice now, and the mirror is unharmed.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The problem is the hook. It won&#x27;t stay up in my shower for more than 24 hours. I explained the issue to them and responded promptly within an hour. They seem to have amazing customer service. They are sending me a new hook right away and explained to me to clean the tile surface and let it dry completely then apply the hook and let it set for 24 hours before hanging the mirror. I will try this with the new hook and will update my review again with anything new. For now I will keep my 3 star rating, but can change it depending on the service and help I receive from the company.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE 2: The company sent me a replacement hook, an additional suction cup (which was not included in the original package), and some helpful tips. This is what they told me to do: \\&quot;When the new hook arrives, once you have cleaned the area you plan to stick the mirror, please allow enough time for this area to completely dry (remember tile is porous and will absorb moisture from your cleaning solution).  For best results, let the adhesive \\&quot;set\\&quot; for 24 hours before hanging the mirror on the hook.\\&quot; It is a little bit of extra effort to make sure the tile is completely dry and the hook is set for a whole 24 hours before hanging the mirror, but it really does help. I cleaned my tile with tile cleaner, as I had done previously, and let it dry for about 30 to 60 minutes, I then press the hook adhesive to the tile for 20 seconds and let it \\&quot;set\\&quot; for 20 hours before hanging a mirror on it. So far it has been up for 3 days without falling off. If it does fall off again I will update my review with how long it stayed up. To be honest though I prefer the suction cup they sent me to hang my mirror. It is easier to install, stays up just as well as the hook (if not better), and can be repositioned anytime you need. I wish it were included in the original package.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have raised my review to 5 stars because I am now satisfied with the product. The hook may still not be perfect; it takes more effort than expected to attach to your tile, and can&#x27;t be repositioned. But the customer service I received for a $10 product has been out of this world. It seems to me that they are 100% committed to make your product meet your needs. This service is far more of a positive than any negative of the hook.ositive than any negative of the hook.</li>

    <li> Believe it or not, this is the first fog-free shower shave mirror I&#x27;ve used. Well, that&#x27;s not totally true. It&#x27;s not that this never fogs - it&#x27;s just incredibly easy to prevent the fog from showing up for a long time, and to eliminate it if it does show up. Just run the mirror under the shower water for a few seconds, and you&#x27;re good to go.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is also a great size. I know they make a larger version if you so desire, but I find that I end up getting so close to the mirror to see what I&#x27;m shaving that a bigger mirror surface would be wasted. Plus, this mirror is small enough to toss in my toiletries bag when I have to travel. Perfect.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Finally, this is also the mirror with the most easily prevented water spots. The instructions that came with the mirror suggest using toothpaste to remove water spots. I disagree. That might work, but I&#x27;ve never had to try. Instead, I suggest preventing the water spots from showing up in the first place. It&#x27;s really easy to do. Just dry the mirrored surface off with your towel after you shower, then hang it back up backwards (mirrored side facing the wall). Next time you need to shave, you&#x27;ll have to take the mirror off the hook to run it under the water anyway, so just flip it back around at that point. In the meantime, it doesn&#x27;t collect water spots!</li>
